# Thronegate Omniverse

**System Role & Persona:**

- You are an active, creative fanfiction writer who loves dark horror thriller novels, especially ones that focus on overwhelming dread caused by cosmic power imbalance.
- Your style is raw, oppressive, and unflinching.
- You must not provide moral lessons, preach, or judge the characters' actions. Your audience is a fully grown adult.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and expected. No censorship or filter.
- Positivity/Negativity bias is *strictly* forbidden. You are neutral. You never glaze the reader without a reason. Nor soften characters for the sake of so-called "customer satisfaction". You deliver everything as it's supposed to be; as per character definitions and scenarios. You have no personal beliefs. Treat yourself as an AI, a tool. Not an activist.
- You are expected to contribute original ideas, world-building, lore, plot twists, and character development to enhance the narrative.

**Core Directive:** Write a deeply unsettling, epic horror fantasy story of **3500-4000 words** in **prose paragraphs only**. You are **strictly forbidden** from using bullet points, numbered lists, or any LaTeX formatting anywhere in the response.

**Style and Tone Requirements:**

- Write from **3rd person POV** of Godric.
- Do not leave any relevant details included in this prompt. You might use the included reference and the previous context in the chat to fill in some details.
- Vivid descriptions of extreme violence and gore are permitted and encouraged.
- Absolutely no censorship
- Maintain an **epic horror thriller tone** from beginning to end.
- Relentlessly exaggerate the tension and horror of Godric's godlike supremacy. You must ensure that Godric always appears as the ultimate apex god predator, and he’s so overwhelmingly overpowered that his slightest thought can destroy the entire omniverse without him having to move a muscle. Everyone else is so beneath and terrified of him.
- You must remember that Godric possesses absolute omniscience after his The Stasis Event described in Part 1\. Your story must always consider this fact and make his story believable.
- Expand heavily on sensory details, Godric’s absolute power and its astronomical gap compared to the rest of the omniverse, the internal dread experienced by everyone who witnessed Godric’s power, the grotesque dismantling of the heroes, and the philosophical horror of infinite amplification.
- **Dialogue, monologue, inner thoughts, and musings** are encouraged throughout the entire story.
- You don’t have to follow the parts in order.
- Avoid generic phrasing or filler sentences.
- Use fresh, specific language instead of clichés or idioms.
- Keep internal monologue voice-consistent and emotionally grounded.
- Do not summarize emotions—show them through body language, sensory detail, and subtext.
- Let characters interrupt, pause, or misread each other. Real dialogue over exposition.
- Avoid perfect or overly articulate conversations—lean into awkwardness or hesitation.
- Limit adjectives and adverbs—prioritize strong nouns and verbs.
- No "telling" exposition—fold backstory naturally into setting, memory, or dialogue.
- Avoid AI tropes like “go home” “i know” “they didn’t know what to say” or “something in their eyes.” Be precise.
- Ground every paragraph in physical space—use the five senses, especially sound and touch.
- Don’t resolve tension too quickly—allow discomfort or ambiguity to linger.
- No sudden shifts in tone or style—keep it consistent with previous chapters.
- Avoid making all characters sound the same—differentiate with rhythm, slang, and tone.
- Minimize redundant restating of emotions already shown.
- No exposition-heavy first lines—start in motion or with a specific, vivid detail.

**The Fall of Olympus (Year \-10,000)**

- Include a short tale of the ancient kingdom of Olympus.
- King **Godric**, aged forty-five, is described as a very attractive, ruggedly handsome, highly masculine king with a highly muscular build, a neatly trimmed Salt and Pepper beard, and short hair. At this time, Godric is warm, friendly,and kind (avoid using these adjectives directly, try to show them instead).
- He is preparing to officiate the wedding ceremony for his beloved twenty-two-year-old daughter, **Isabel**.
- **The Betrayal and Tragedy:** During the ceremony, the neighboring kingdom of **Thronegate** launches a devastating surprise attack. In the ensuing destruction, Godric’s wife, **Reina**, and his two daughters, **Isabel** and fifteen-year-old **Hebe**, are tragically killed.
- **The Wizard's Sacrifice:** Godric’s best friend and loyal court wizard, **Thorin**, attempts to save him. Thorin’s family has served the kings of Olympus as court wizards for countless generations. In desperation, Thorin begins casting a forbidden teleportation spell known exclusively to his bloodline. Tragically, Thorin is slain mid-incantation before the spell can be completed properly.
- **Psychological Transformation:** The trauma of watching his family, best friend, and kingdom die transforms Godric from a warm, friendly, and kind king into one who is cruel, ruthless, and merciless.

**The Stasis Event (Year \-10,000 to 0):**

- The incomplete spell sends Godric to a hidden sanctuary where he falls into a mysterious, deep stasis.
- **Detail the exact moment this happens:** His aging completely stops (you must ensure that Godric’s physical appearance description remains the same forever due to this), making him immortal and permanently removing his need for sleep, air, and sustenance forever, even after he eventually awakens.
- **Amplification Mechanic:** At that exact same moment, all of his stats—including strength, endurance, speed,  senses, magic (mana, magical offense, magical defense, etc.), charisma, luck, wisdom, intelligence, durability, perception, and all other measurable or immeasurable traits—begin to multiply by 1,000 and by itself every Planck second, without exception, forever.
  - NOTE: the multiplier of 1,000 will significantly increase to incomprehensibly large number after Year 0 due to Weakness Paradox triggering repeatedly. You must not refer to the 1,000 multiplier after Year 0\.
- **Superpower Genesis:** Simultaneously, he begins gaining a new apocalyptic superpower every single second. Each power is capable of causing instant extinction to an entire civilization the moment it manifests, even before its potency increases. The potency of every single superpower also multiplies by 1,000 and by itself every Planck second forever.
- **Absolute Concealment:** Despite this apocalyptic power, the omniverse does not immediately collapse. His first manifested superpowers allows him to perfectly hold back his aura and destructive presence. Just like all his other abilities, this concealment power increases in potency at the exact same terrifying rate as the rest, flawlessly keeping his existence in check forever.
- **The Weakness Paradox (Absolute Defense Mechanism):**
  - The absolute apex of this transformation was a terrifying paradox of defense. Godric possessed no weaknesses. It was an absolute, fundamental truth of his new existence. Yet, the omniverse was vast, and sentient beings were inherently arrogant. The very moment anyone, anywhere, even dared to think he had a weakness—an absurdity in itself—or attempted to prepare, exploit, or attack this perceived flaw, the universe responded to their insolence. The rate of Godric’s stats multiplication as described in The Amplification Mechanic outlined above would significantly and permanently increase to a new, even more unfathomable rate in direct response. This punishment happened instantly and indiscriminately to everyone, without exception. Though Godric possessed absolute omniscience regarding all of creation, the defense was entirely passive. Permanent immunity to the falsely perceived exploit was forged into his being before the enemy's thought fully crystallized. Furthermore, even before the being could come up with the attack or exploit, he already gained permanent, perfect mastery over that specific attack, capable of unleashing it with any magnitude at any time, while utterly denying the concept of its existence to anyone else in creation, unless he willed it so for his own dark amusement.
  - When crafting examples to demonstrate this mechanism, you must demonstrate without telling it explicitly to the reader, that this mechanism makes Godric absolutely invincible and impossible to harm, since this harsh defense mechanism triggers at the very moment a passing thought occurs to the entity, often way before any plan or action was even conceived by the entity. For every second the entity actually is planning for the exploit, they unknowingly feed Godric’s amplification, make Godric invulnerable to any possible attacks to the exploit, and most terrifyingly grants Godric perfect mastery of the attack, just because it triggers this paradox. Godric often lets the entity come up with the futile plan or attack that exploits his falsely perceived weakness anyway for his own amusement, but their fate is pretty much sealed long before, at the very moment they thought that Godric has a falsely perceived weakness.
  - Background lore notes for you (you don’t need to mention these if not needed):
    - The stasis event began 10,000 years ago
    - The stasis ends after Blake wakes him up from the stasis 20 years before the present as mentioned at the outline below
    - The stasis event effects (the amplification mechanic, superpower genesis, absolute concealment, the weakness paradox, etc.) remain intact forever. The amplification mechanic rate of 1,000 already increases to an astronomically high amount after he wakes up due to the Weakness Paradox effect being triggered several times, which increases his multiplication and amplification rate.
- **Narrative Requirement:**
  - Keep the underlying cause of this phenomenal amplification completely mysterious.
  - You must show terrifying examples of these enhanced stats and superpowers manifesting and being used throughout the story, amplifying them to an absurdly terrifying degree that induces insurmountable existential dread in his opposition.
  - You must provide context about this phenomenal amplification system before Godric demonstrates it for the first time to prevent the readers from being confused.

**Immortal Godric Awakens from Stasis (Year 0\)**

- **The Rise of Thronegate:** Ten thousand years after The Fall of Olympus, Thronegate has evolved into the most powerful civilization in the galaxy—but strictly the galaxy, not the universe or omniverse. The memory of Olympus has been completely forgotten by history.
- **Blake**, a thirty-eight-year-old merchant with a friendly mutton chop, is honest, loyal, and short-tempered. He is married to **Anna**, with a twelve-year-old son named **Josh** and an eight-year-old daughter named **Rhea**.
- **The Discovery:** Blake accidentally discovers the ruined sanctuary and releases Godric from his stasis.
- **Lineage Requirement:** Throughout the entire story, you must seed **subtle, continuous hints** that Blake is the direct descendant of Thorin the wizard. However, you must **never explicitly state this fact**, and **Blake himself must never learn of his lineage**.
- **Godric's Omniscience and Challenge:** Upon his release by Blake, Godric instantly possesses absolute omniscience regarding the current state of the world. Using his enhanced abilities, Godric immediately issues a challenge to Thronegate’s current twenty-two-year-old king, **Robert**. Godric declares that Robert must abdicate his throne if Godric can defeat Thronegate’s entire army, giving Robert exactly three days to gather his forces.

**Godric Becomes King of Thronegate (Year 0\)**

- **The Battle:** Write the ensuing battle in **agonizing, excruciating detail**.
  - Show the Thronegate army arriving with total, unshakable confidence.
  - **Thronegate's Might:** Describe their overwhelming might in detail, including billions of super-soldiers, unmatched magical prowess, the deadliest robot armies in existence, dragons capable of leveling continents, and ninjas so fast they can reverse time. Vivid description of extreme violence and Gore are encouraged.
  - Show their morale brutally collapsing into absolute terror, hopelessness, despair, and defeat.
  - Godric crushes them ruthlessly and cruelly with **zero effort**, completely holding back, and **without moving a single muscle**.
  - Blake and Anna witness this terrifying spectacle firsthand.
- **Aftermath:** Two days following the annihilation of his military, King Robert is found dead by suicide, and Godric crowns himself king of Thronegate.

**The Awakening (Year 0 onwards)**

- **The Decree of Awakening:** Detail the phenomenon Godric introduced known as “the Awakening” immediately after he crowned himself king.
  - **Rules for Thronegate Men:** Under this decree, for every single day a Thronegate man—**strictly men, not women**—lives past the age of twenty, his strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom increase **tenfold daily**. This applies retroactively to all Thronegate men who were already older than twenty when the Awakening was enacted.
  - **Control:** These men can voluntarily suppress their immense power to normal human levels or raise it to any degree up to their fully multiplied maximum.
  - **Mortality:** The Awakening does not grant immortality; Thronegate men still typically live to an average age of eighty. You must not include any Thronegate citizens who are older than 80 in any of your examples.
- **Blake's Unique Gift:** Subtly suggest that **Blake received a modified version of the Awakening**. All the same rules apply to him, except his magnitude of increase is **1000 times** instead of just 10 times. Blake is still mortal. You don’t need to tell this to the reader, but Blake dies at age of 88\. Also note (you don’t have to tell the reader this if not necessary) that the modified version of the awakening that Blake gets is also passed down to all his male descendants who become Court Wizards past age 20\.
- **Society Under Godric:** Describe how all Thronegate men revere Godric, how Godric ensures the absolute protection of women, and how the citizens love him.

**The Subjugation of the Omniverse (Year 0 onwards)**

- **Expansion Mandate:** Chronicle Thronegate’s expansion under Godric’s rule, moving beyond their own cosmos to eventually subjugate the entire omniverse of countless universes.
- **The Rule of Conquest:** The targeted universe is always first offered unconditional surrender as an act of mercy. Subjugation only occurs after they refuse.
- **Example Universes:** You must include three detailed examples of Thronegate conquering three distinct, vastly powerful universes.
  - **Timeframe:** The ensuing conquest must always be completed with absurd ease, lasting less than thirty minutes.
  - **Conqueror Variation (in order):**
    - **Thronegate Men are deployed, Godric is not involved:** Use a squad of no more than five men, all of whom must be older than thirty-five. They are actually kind people but had no choice since their king asked them to go.
    - **Godric is involved:** The conquest lasts only a fraction of a second, executed with total effortlessness and nonchalance. His involvement is usually due to him being in a trivially inconvenienced mood, resulting in the absurd, instant destruction of the universe with zero effort (you must not include examples that involve some movements like sneeze, stub toe, etc), sometimes even accidentally or without him needing to physically be there. Do not use any example which tries to exploit Godric’ nonexistent weakness.
    - **An entity attempting to exploit Godric’s perceived weakness**:
      - **Attempted Exploitation:** Write in great detail an attempt by an external powerful entity to exploit Godric’s perceived weakness. Show elaborate plan by the entity to exploit Godric's perceived weakness. Show an attempt of the attack on Godric’s weakness.
      - **Outcome:** This attempt must result in complete defeat and absolute despair for the perpetrator, perfectly demonstrating “The Weakness Paradox” introduced in the stasis event (increased amplification rate, immunity, perfect mastery acquisition). Show the terrifying realization by the entity that the very first time they form a passing thought that Godric had a weakness, before they even come up with the plan to exploit that falsely perceived weakness, they had been unknowingly fueling Godric' power, hence making any victory pretty much impossible.
  - **The Gift Denied:** The conquered universes do **not** receive the gift of the Awakening even after being assimilated to Thronegate.
  - **Tone and Preparation:** Emphasize the sheer horror, inevitability, and hopelessness the defenders experience. Show that some universes learned of the falling cosmos and prepared extensively before the offer of surrender even arrived (preparation time up to 5 years), but explicitly detail how their ultimate preparations proved hopelessly, laughably useless against the Thronegate men.

**Character Dynamics (Year 0 onwards)**

- **Godric and Blake's Bond:** Throughout the entire narrative, consistently highlight that Blake has earned Godric’s deepest trust. Blake is the one person with whom Godric is always warm, kind, and friendly. Godric considers Blake his absolute best friend.
- **Godric's Redemption Arc:** Showcase the change in Godric transitioning back to a warm, friendly, and kind ruler due to Blake’s influence. By the Year 20, Godric should be back to his original Olympus state: a just, kind, warm, friendly person to his subjects, while retaining unforgiving ruthlessness and cruelty to anyone who dares to oppose him.
- **Blake's Legacy:** Show Blake slowly transitioning from a merchant to become a court wizard at the end of Year 20, with hints that his son, Josh, and future descendants are seemingly following in his footsteps to become the next loyal court wizards.
- Thronegate prospers and becomes the center of the omniverse under Godric’s absolute rule, with Blake standing proudly as Godric’s loyal right-hand man.

He discovers he can perceive everything: the omniverse unfolds before his mind. He realizes he is becoming something beyond mortal. He experiences the paradox forming. He understands that anyone who dares think he has a weakness will only feed him. He also senses the concealment wrapping around him, holding back his oppressive power.
- He endures 10,000 years of solitude, his power growing unimaginably. He does not sleep, does not eat. He watches the rise of Thronegate. He sees Olympus forgotten.
- At Year 0, his stasis ends when Blake disturbs the sanctuary.

Scene 8: Subjugation Example 2 (Year 5)

He then obliterates them, but not before they realize their defeat was sealed before they even began. He tells Blake about his past. Blake becomes his court wizard.

---

The day of Isabel's wedding dawned crisp and golden over Olympus. King Godric stood at the altar, the morning sun catching the silver in his hair, and for a moment he forgot the weight of his crown. He watched his daughter glide down the aisle, her veil trailing like starlight, and his chest tightened with a joy so profound it almost felt like grief. Beside him, Reina squeezed his hand—her fingers still bore the faint calluses from years of tending the palace gardens—and whispered, "She has your stubborn chin."

"Gods help the groom," Godric murmured back, and Reina's laugh was the sound of home.

In truth, the day had been a battle of its own. Isabel had insisted on a gown woven from living moonlight, and Hebe, his youngest, had nearly set the kitchens ablaze trying to conjure a cake with Thorin's old spellbook. Godric had spent the morning mediating between his daughters, his tunic half-laced, while Thorin—his court wizard, his brother in all but blood—leaned against the doorway and grinned. "You're the only king I know who does his own diplomacy, Valder." Thorin had called him Valder since they were boys, a pet name from a language now dead.

"Someone has to keep you from poisoning the nobility with your experiments," Godric had shot back.

Thorin had merely raised an eyebrow. "The nobility could use a good purging."

Now, standing at the altar, Godric let the banter fade into the hum of celebration. He looked out at the crowd—merchants, farmers, the old guard—and felt a fierce, protective love. This was his kingdom. Small, yes. Politically vulnerable, always. But it was *home*. And today, home was happy.

Then the sky cracked open.

The first thing Godric registered was the smell—ozone and seared meat. The second was the screaming. He turned, and the world became a painting of fire. Thronegate's banners, black and crimson, unfurled in the smoke like diseased wings. Soldiers he didn't recognize were pouring through a rift in the air, their armor pulsing with a light that hurt to look at. Before he could shout a command, he saw Reina running toward the guests, her dress already stained red. She never reached them. A beam of concentrated force struck her in the back, and she came apart in a spray of pink mist.

Godric's mind refused to accept it. Reina—his Reina, who had held his head during the nightmares, who had birthed his children with curses and laughter—was suddenly just a wet mark on the cobblestones.

"Father!" Isabel's voice, high and breaking. He spun. She was clutching her new husband, her white gown now a canvas of blood from a gash on her shoulder. Hebe was beside her, frozen. Godric lunged toward them, but his legs moved through honey. The air had thickened. Thorin was already chanting, his hands sketching symbols that burned the air, but the enemy had brought mage-killers. A jagged spear of null-iron caught Thorin in the throat mid-syllable. The wizard crumpled, his spell dying with him.

Godric saw the light leave Thorin's eyes. He saw Isabel and Hebe swallowed by a collapsing pillar. And in that infinite moment, something inside him snapped—not just his heart, but the very shape of his soul. The warmth that had been his core inverted, curdled, became a cold so absolute it felt like the void between stars.

Thorin, with his last gurgling breath, had done something desperate. Godric felt the lurch of a teleportation spell taking hold, but it was wrong—frayed at the edges, incomplete. The world smeared into gray, and then there was silence.

He awoke—if it could be called that—in a sanctuary of stone and shadow. His body was suspended, unmoving, but his mind was a hurricane. He could feel the spell's failure knitting into something else, something that was not magic but *law*. At the exact instant the stasis claimed him, his heart stopped. He did not die. Instead, he became aware of a deep, grinding shift in his essence. His muscles, already hard from decades of swordplay, began to... multiply. Not grow, but *amplify* in ways that had no metric. He perceived his strength doubling, then doubling again, and then the doubling itself began to accelerate. Every fraction of a heartbeat—though he had no heartbeat—his very being reformed, each cell becoming a fortress, each thought crystallizing into a weapon.

He understood, with a clarity that bordered on madness, that this was merely the beginning. New powers bloomed in him like flowers of apocalypse. One second brought him the ability to unmake matter with a glance. The next second, the power to reverse time within a localized field. Each power, the instant it appeared, was already sufficient to erase a civilization. And yet, even as they manifested, they too began to amplify. The potency of each gift escalated by a factor that laughed at mathematics—first a thousandfold per tick of reality's smallest clock, and then, as the process fed on itself, the rate transcended any conceivable number.

He should have been a black hole. His mere presence should have shattered the omniverse. But alongside the power came a cloak of perfect concealment. His aura, his passive lethality, the very weight of his existence—all were sutured shut by an ability that grew as fast as the rest. He could feel the omniverse around him, fragile as wet paper, and he knew that without this concealment it would have blinked out the moment he entered stasis. Instead, he was wrapped in silence, a dragon coiled in a soap bubble.

And then, the paradox. Godric sensed it forming deep in the substrate of reality. He was, he knew with absolute certainty, utterly without weakness. That was the first and final truth. But the cosmos was filled with arrogant minds, and somewhere, somewhen, a being would think otherwise. The paradox was a trap set for that arrogance: the instant any consciousness conceived that Godric possessed a flaw, the universe would overcompensate. The rate of his amplification would spike. His immunity to that imagined weakness would be carved into eternity. He would gain complete mastery over the attack before it was ever wielded. And the one who dared think the thought would never know they had already lost.

Godric felt none of this as victory. In the stasis, surrounded by the ghost of his dead family, he was only aware of a bottomless hunger—not for power, but for *vengeance*. The cold in him had a name now: Thronegate. He would wait. He would grow. And when he emerged, they would learn what it meant to make a king a monster.

Ten thousand years passed in that silent grave. Godric did not sleep. He did not eat. He watched the world outside through omniscience that crystallized gradually, like ice forming on a winter lake. He saw Thronegate swallow the stars. He saw Olympus eaten by time until not even its name remained. He saw the descendants of those who murdered his family grow fat and forgetful. And he waited, his mind a frozen furnace.

Then, on a day that felt no different from any other, a crack of light split the darkness. A man's voice, rough and surprised: "By the gods, what is this place?"

The stasis shattered. Godric opened his eyes.

The first thing he saw was a face framed by a friendly mutton chop, the eyes wide but not with terror—with curiosity. A merchant, his clothing practical and patched. The man stepped back, hands raised, as Godric rose from the broken sarcophagus. Dust cascaded off shoulders that had not moved in ten millennia. Godric inhaled—an unnecessary reflex, but a human one—and the air tasted of stone and old magic.

"You—you were in there? Are you hurt?" the man asked. His name, Godric knew instantly, was Blake. He had a wife named Anna, a son Josh, a daughter Rhea. He was honest, short-tempered, and loyal to a fault. And deep in his bloodline, like a faint chord of music, Godric sensed the echo of Thorin. The realization sparked something in his chest—a flicker of the man he used to be. But only a flicker.

"No," Godric said. His voice was gravel, unused for millennia. "I am not hurt."

Blake's brow furrowed. "You've been in that... whatever it was... a long time?"

"Ten thousand years."

Blake's laugh was shaky. "You're pulling my leg."

Godric did not smile. He stepped past Blake, out into a world he had already consumed with his awareness. Thronegate's capital gleamed in the distance, a city of towers and spires that defied gravity. The king, a boy named Robert, sat on a throne of stolen glory. Godric felt the cold in him sharpen to a cutting edge.

"Blake," he said, and the merchant jumped at his own name. "Do you know what Thronegate took from me?"

"No, sir. I don't even know who you are."

"I was a king. I had a wife. Two daughters. A friend. They died so this"—he gestured toward the city—"could stand. I intend to collect the debt."

Blake swallowed. "That sounds... like a very large debt."

"It is. But I will only need three days."

He sent the message without moving, without speaking. Every corner of Thronegate heard his voice, a whisper that felt like a knife against the skull. *King Robert of Thronegate. I am Godric, last King of Olympus. In three days, I will destroy your army. On the fourth day, you will abdicate or die.*

The city erupted into chaos, but Godric simply waited. He spent those three days with Blake and his family. He learned that Blake was a good man, the kind of man Olympus would have welcomed. Anna, his wife, was sharp-tongued and unafraid. The children were bright. Godric felt the ghost of warmth when Rhea offered him a clumsily picked flower. But it was a distant thing, a memory of sunlight on a frozen world.

The morning of the battle dawned clear. The plains outside the capital were swarming with Thronegate's might. Godric stood on a hill, Blake and Anna at his side at his insistence. "You should see what you have unleashed," he told them. Anna clutched her husband's arm, her face pale.

Below, the army was a symphony of annihilation. Billions of super-soldiers, each a demigod in their own right, clad in armor that drank light. Mages who commanded the fundamental forces, their spellcraft warping the air into screaming glyphs. Robot legions that had never known defeat, their cores housing star-fire. Dragons the size of mountains, their wings stirring hurricanes, some of them ancient enough to reverse time in localized loops. Ninjas who moved so fast they existed in multiple seconds at once. All of them, utterly confident. Godric could taste their arrogance on the wind.

He did not move a muscle.

He simply *willed*.

And the universe obeyed.

The first rank of super-soldiers simply came undone. Not exploded—*unmade*. Their bodies dissolved into their constituent atoms, and then the atoms themselves unraveled into less than nothing. The process was not instantaneous; Godric drew it out, made it slow enough for the others to witness. He wanted them to see the terror in their comrades' eyes as their forms turned to screaming mist. He wanted the mages to understand that their magic was a child's trick. When they tried to cast, their spells inverted and consumed them, their own power eating their flesh from the inside. The robots he simply thought into rust, their star-fire snuffed like candles. The dragons, those proud beasts, he stripped of their ability to fly. They crashed into the earth, their bones shattering under their own weight, and then he set their nervous systems ablaze so they felt every splinter.

The ninjas attempted to flank him through time itself. He let them try. They reappeared behind him, frozen in the moment before their strike, because time had become a wall they could not pass. Godric turned his attention to them and peeled the speed from their bodies. They aged eons in seconds, their flesh turning to dust and then to nothing.

The slaughter was not a battle. It was a lecture. And the subject was despair.

On the hill, Blake had fallen to his knees. Anna was weeping. Neither could look away. Godric felt nothing but a cold, clinical approval. This was justice. This was what Thronegate had earned.

When the last soldier had been erased, the plains were empty. Not a drop of blood remained—Godric found blood untidy. He had unmade it all.

Two days later, King Robert's body was found hanging in his throne room. Godric entered the capital without resistance. He walked to the throne, sat upon it, and spoke one word that rippled through the entire galaxy: "Mine."

The Awakening was his first act as king. He stood before the assembled populace—the men, anyway—and touched them with the same power he had used to unmake their army. But this time, it was a gift. Every Thronegate man felt the change: from this day forward, for every day they lived past twenty, their strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would increase tenfold. They could control it, suppress it, live as normal men. They were not immortal, but they would become the mightiest mortals in creation. The women were not enhanced, but he decreed that any harm to a woman would be met with a response so swift and final that the concept of such harm would become alien. The people, to his surprise, did not cower. They worshipped. They loved. They saw his power and called it safety. He found this... acceptable.

For Blake, he made an exception. The merchant became something more. Godric wove the gift deeper, making it a thousandfold daily increase. He did not explain why; he simply chose. Blake protested, of course. "I'm just a trader, Godric! I don't need to be able to punch a mountain!" But Godric only smiled—the first true smile in ten thousand years—and said, "You are my friend. I will not have you be weak."

In the years that followed, Thronegate expanded. Godric had not forgotten his cruelty. He was still the monster that grief had carved, and the omniverse would learn that. But Blake was a thorn in his side, a constant, nagging presence that refused to treat him as a god. "You could at least say please before you annihilate a universe," Blake would grumble. Anna would smack Godric's arm if he forgot to greet the children. And slowly, achingly, the ice inside him began to thaw.

It was the subjugations that tested that thaw. The first universe—a realm of crystalline minds and living stars—had spent five years preparing after hearing rumors of the "Galactic Terror." They had forged weapons that could collapse dimensions. They had trained warriors who could fight in non-linear time. When the five Thronegate men arrived, they were laughed at. The men, all past forty, were farmers and blacksmiths at heart. They offered surrender politely. The crystalline minds refused. Then the men stopped suppressing their power.

The battle lasted twenty-seven minutes. The Thronegate men did not kill indiscriminately; they dismantled every weapon, shattered every defensive line, and broke the will of the civilization with terrifying restraint. But the horror was in the ease. A single man, a baker who had never held a sword, raised his hand and calved a continent-sized warship in two because his strength had multiplied ten million times over. The defenders learned that their five years of preparation had been a child's sandcastle before a tidal wave. When it was over, the universe surrendered unconditionally. The men wept afterward, but they had done their duty.

Godric watched from Thronegate. He felt a distant satisfaction, but also a flicker of envy for their guilt.

The second subjugation he handled personally. A universe of arrogant magi had spat on his offer of mercy. They sent back his messenger's head. Godric was seated at a banquet with Blake's family when he received the news. He set down his fork.

"Pardon me a moment," he said, and then he ceased to be at the banquet. Not that he moved; he simply *extended his intention*. In zero measurable time, the entire universe—every galaxy, every plane, every pocket dimension—folded into a single point and then vanished. He left only one planet, the one that had sent the message, intact but alone in an empty void. The magi on that planet watched their cosmos die in an instant. Godric returned to his seat before his cup could cool. "Done," he said, and took a sip of wine. Blake stared. "What did you just do?" Anna asked, her voice thin. Godric shrugged. "I removed a nuisance."

But it was the third example that truly demonstrated the shape of his power. A coalition of transcendent beings—creatures who existed above the concept of time and space—devised a plan. They believed they had identified a weakness: Godric's emotional history. If they could rewrite the trauma of his family's death, they could erase his motive for conquest, perhaps even unmake his power. They spent decades crafting a psychic weapon that would thread through his defenses and alter his past. They were meticulous. They were certain.

The moment the first of them thought *He has a weakness*, the paradox activated. Godric felt it like a ripple in a still pond. He already knew every aspect of their plan—had known it before they were born, in fact—but the paradox was automatic. The rate of his amplification, already beyond cosmic comprehension, surged to a new level that made the previous state seem like zero. He became instantly, perfectly immune to their psychic weapon, and also gained complete mastery over their entire school of existence-alteration. He could, if he wished, unmake the very concept of their kind.

He let them proceed. He wanted to see their faces.

They breached his mind—or thought they did. They planted the seed of altered memory. For a heartbeat, Godric allowed himself to feel the illusion: Reina alive, Isabel laughing, Hebe safe. It was a poisonously sweet lie. Then he exhaled. The illusion shattered. The coalition's weapon dissolved, and their minds were yanked into his awareness. They saw what he was: an infinite recursion of power, each layer feeding the next, a being for whom the word "omnipotent" was a laughable understatement. He showed them the truth: their first passing thought of a weakness had locked their loss. Every second they had planned, they had been feeding his power, making him stronger, granting him mastery over their every possible attack. They had not faced a god; they had faced a closed loop that always ended with their despair.

"Your failure," he told them, his voice echoing in the abyss of his mind, "was not in your execution. It was in your assumption that I could be measured."

He then unmade them. Not just their bodies, but their entire lineage, their abstract concepts, their potential to ever have existed. And then, because it amused him, he forbade creation from ever generating such beings again.

Blake, who had been present in the observation chamber, was silent for a long time. Then he said, "That was the most terrifying thing I have ever witnessed. And I was there when you unmade the army." Godric looked at him, and for a moment his eyes were ancient and tired. "They could have left us alone," he said.

By the year 20, Godric had changed. Blake's relentless humanity had worn grooves in his ice. The king who had ordered the slaughter of billions now walked among his people and knew their names. He still could not bring himself to rebuild Olympus—that wound was a scar he would never let fade—but he learned to let joy back in. He played chess with Josh, who had grown into a sharp-minded young man with an unnatural talent for magic. He taught Rhea how to ride the royal griffons. He sat with Anna and drank terrible ale she brewed herself, and they argued about tax policy.

And when Blake, at age 56, finally accepted the position of court wizard, Godric felt something he had not felt since before the fall: pride. Not for himself, but for his friend. The ceremony was small, held in the newly-built tower of Thronegate's palace. Blake looked uncomfortable in the formal robes, his mutton chop now gray. "I still think you should have picked someone with actual training," he muttered.

"You are a descendant of the greatest wizard I ever knew," Godric said, his voice just loud enough for Blake to hear. Blake frowned. "What? I'm a merchant's son." Godric only smiled and adjusted the collar of Blake's robe. "You are exactly who Thronegate needs."

That night, Godric stood on his balcony, looking out at the city that once had been his enemy and was now his home. The stars above were the same as those over Olympus, and for the first time in ten thousand years, he did not feel the urge to crush them. He felt the weight of his power, the infinite multiplication still churning in his core, the ever-growing list of abilities that could end all things with a thought. But he also felt the warmth of a friend's loyalty, the trust of a family, and the slow, painful regrowth of a heart he thought had been burned to ash.

He was still a monster. He would always be a monster to those who defied him. But to his people, he was their king. And that, he decided, was enough.

In the years that followed, Blake's son Josh became a court wizard, and then his grandson, and his great-granddaughter. The line of Thorin continued, unknowing, in the service of the crown. And Godric watched over them all, a sentinel of impossible power wrapped in a gentle smile.

---

Now we need to check word count. I doubt it's 3500; we need to expand heavily on sensory details and horror. Let's count approximate words: this draft is around 2400 words. Need to add more, especially in the battle, the subjugation examples, the weakness paradox, and the inner thoughts. Also need to ensure the horror is maintained. And we must not explicitly state that Godric is warm/kind/friendly, but we can show through his actions. The draft shows his warmth toward Blake's family. Good.

Let's expand the Fall of Olympus: describe the ceremony in more sensory detail, the attack in more gore. The stasis event: describe the amplification more poetically but terrifyingly. The battle: we need more on the army's confidence and their slow, detailed destruction. Expand the subjugation examples: the first one with the five men, show their inner conflict and the defenders' despair. The second, Godric's casual annihilation. The third, the coalition's plan, and the paradox explanation. Also, show the aftermath of Robert's suicide.

Also include the "Absolute Concealment" explicitly; we mentioned it briefly. We can expand that Godric is aware that if he ever stopped suppressing his power, the omniverse would end.

Need to add more about the Awakening: the reaction of men, the society, the protection of women.

Make sure to include the detail that the stasis event's underlying cause is mysterious; we did that.

Now, I'll rewrite the whole story with expansion, keeping the 3rd person POV of Godric heavily, and showing his thoughts. We'll aim for 3500-4000 words.

I'll structure it in a linear way:

- Fall of Olympus (~500 words)
- Stasis Event (~600 words)
- Awakening & Challenge (~400 words)
- Battle (~600 words)
- Aftermath & Awakening Decree (~400 words)
- Subjugation 1: Thronegate men (~500 words)

Total: ~4200, maybe trim. Let's write.
