                    "text": "The morning of Isabel\u2019s wedding, Godric stood before the tall mirror in his chambers and practiced his smile. Not because the joy was false\u2014his heart was a hive of it, buzzing so loudly he could barely think\u2014but because he wanted to be sure the expression was right. When his daughter looked up at him from the altar, he wanted her to see every hour he\u2019d spent teaching her to ride, every scraped knee he\u2019d kissed, every nightmare he\u2019d chased away. The smile needed to hold all of that.\n\nHe adjusted the golden clasp at his shoulder. Reina had pressed it into his palm that morning, her fingers smelling of rosemary from the kitchen garden she insisted on tending herself. \u201cIt belonged to my father,\u201d she\u2019d said, \u201cand his before him. They\u2019d want you to wear it today.\u201d Godric had kissed her forehead\u2014her skin was still cool from the well water\u2014and promised not to lose it. Behind him, Hebe burst through the door, her braids already unraveling. \u201cPapa! Aunt Miren says I can\u2019t wear my training boots to the ceremony, but they\u2019re lucky boots!\u201d Godric scooped her up, ignoring the protest of his formal tunic, and carried her to the window. \u201cYou can wear one lucky boot,\u201d he negotiated, \u201cif you promise not to levitate the cake again.\u201d Hebe\u2019s grin was a sunburst. \u201cDeal.\u201d\n\nThorin appeared moments later, leaning against the doorframe in robes that, for once, weren\u2019t singed. \u201cYou do realize Isabel is the one getting married, not you, Valder.\u201d The old nickname was a comfort, a thread to their boyhood. Godric set Hebe down and clapped his friend on the shoulder. \u201cI\u2019m the king. I\u2019m allowed to preen. Is the spellwork ready?\u201d Thorin\u2019s expression flickered\u2014something dark, quickly hidden. \u201cThe sanctuary ward is set, though I pray we never need it. Today should be about joy.\u201d Godric nodded, and together they walked to the temple courtyard.\n\nThe day was perfect, the sky a hard blue porcelain, the air thick with jasmine from the garlands draped over every arch. Guests filled the stone benches, their finery a patchwork of Olympus\u2019s noble houses. Godric saw Reina in the front row, her dark hair loose, her hand resting on Isabel\u2019s shoulder as the bride adjusted her veil. Hebe was already fidgeting, one foot clad in a scuffed leather boot. Isabel herself was a vision of living moonlight, a gown Thorin had spent months weaving from captured starlight, and when she looked at her father, her smile was the same one she\u2019d worn as a girl bringing him a muddy flower.\n\nGodric took his place at the altar, opened the ancient book of rites, and began. \u201cWe gather today under the eyes of the old gods and the new, to witness the binding of two souls\u2026\u201d His voice was steady, deep, and for a handful of perfect minutes, the world was exactly as it should be.\n\nThen the sky screamed.\n\nIt was a literal sound: a tearing of the atmosphere as a rift of black lightning split the blue from horizon to horizon. The wind died. The birds fell. From the rift poured shapes in armor that drank light, their faces hidden behind helms of null-iron. Thronegate. Neighbors. Allies, or so the treaties claimed. The first blast hit the guest benches before Godric could move. People he\u2019d known for decades\u2014Lord Aeric, who had taught him cards; Lady Mirra, who had nursed him through a fever\u2014became black outlines and then ash, their deaths a wet sizzle that branded itself into his ears.\n\nReina was on her feet, her mouth open in a scream he couldn\u2019t hear over the roar of collapsing stone. A second beam, a sickly violet, carved through the space between her ribs. Godric saw the light enter her chest and exit her back, and he saw the two halves of her body separate in a spray of pink. She never made a sound. She just\u2026 divided. His mind rejected it. She had been speaking a moment ago. Now she was meat on the cobblestones.\n\nHe turned, still running through an invisible resistance, toward his daughters. Isabel had frozen, her new husband\u2019s hand in hers. Hebe was pressed against her sister, her face blank. Godric was ten feet away. Ten feet. And then the third blast fell\u2014a column of white fire that expanded outward. When it retracted, there was only a shallow crater, the edges fused into glass. No bodies. No blood. Just a hole where his children had been.\n\nThe noise that tore from Godric\u2019s throat was not a scream. It was the sound of a foundation cracking. He spun and saw Thorin already casting. The wizard\u2019s hands blazed with crimson sigils\u2014the forbidden teleportation spell of his bloodline, the desperate magic meant to save kings. Godric knew its color, its cost. Thorin\u2019s face was calm, his lips moving faster than sight, but a Thronegate mage-killer, a woman with dead eyes, hurled a null-iron spear. It took Thorin in the throat, pinning him to the altar. Blood sheeted down his chest. His mouth kept working for half a breath, and the spell discharged incomplete.\n\nReality smeared. Godric felt himself wrenched sideways. The last thing he saw was Thorin\u2019s body slumping, and Olympus burning. Then the gray swallowed him, and the cold came.\n\n\u2014\n\nHe did not sleep. The stasis was not unconsciousness; it was an eternity of lucidity in a tomb carved from the bones of a dead star. Godric\u2019s body was suspended in a matrix of amber light, and at the precise instant the teleportation anchored him, every biological function ceased. His heart stopped and did not restart. His lungs stilled. The microscopic machinery of his cells ground to a halt. And in that cessation, a new process ignited.\n\nIt began as a tingle at the base of his skull. Then, in the span of a Planck second\u2014the smallest tick of reality\u2019s clock\u2014his strength multiplied a thousandfold. The next Planck second, that new value multiplied by itself. Then that product multiplied by itself. His endurance, his speed, his senses, his magical capacity, his very charisma and luck\u2014every measurable trait and a thousand immeasurable ones\u2014all began the same recursive escalation. The numbers became meaningless almost instantly. The only truth was that every moment made the last a mockery.\n\nAs the amplification embedded itself, new powers bloomed. One second: the ability to perceive every atom in the omniverse. The next: the ability to command them. Then the power to unmake matter. Then the power to rewrite causality. Then\u2014mercifully\u2014a perfect concealment, a cocoon that held back his passive lethality. Without it, his mere existence would have popped the cosmos like a soap bubble. Each power, at its birth, was already sufficient to end a civilization. And then each power began to amplify just as his base stats had, its potency multiplying by itself every Planck second without end.\n\nBut the true horror was the paradox. As he lay there, growing, Godric became aware of a new absolute: he had no weaknesses. None. It was a fact woven into his new nature. Yet the omniverse was populated by minds that would inevitably perceive weaknesses where none existed. The paradox was a sentinel that preyed on that arrogance. The instant any being, anywhere, conceived that Godric had a flaw\u2014before the thought fully formed, before any plan or weapon existed\u2014his amplification rate would permanently surge. He would gain absolute immunity to that imagined vulnerability. He would gain perfect, godlike mastery over whatever attack or strategy stemmed from it. The thought was the crime, and the punishment was to make him stronger.\n\nHe lay in that frozen amber for ten thousand years, and he felt his mind expand until it held the omniverse like a marble. His omniscience crystallized slowly, a spreading ice of awareness that showed him every hidden plot, every secret motive, every current of suffering. He watched Thronegate rise, swallowing star systems, growing fat on stolen worlds. He watched Olympus erode from memory until even its name was lost. He watched the descendants of his family\u2019s murderers live and die and forget. And all the while, the ice in his chest thickened. The warmth that had been his core became a distant myth. He was vengeance now. A cold, perfect engine of retribution, his every thought a blade waiting to fall.\n\n\u2014\n\nThe year the world called 0\u2014though Godric had stopped counting\u2014a man named Blake blundered into the sanctuary. He was thirty-eight, a merchant with a friendly mutton chop and a short temper, and he was talking before he saw the figure in the amber. \u201c\u2014hell of a find, Anna will never believe\u2014oh! There\u2019s someone in there!\u201d\n\nGodric had known Blake was coming for millennia. He\u2019d watched the man\u2019s lineage stretch back through centuries to a dying wizard in a burning temple. He tasted the old magic in Blake\u2019s blood, the echo of Thorin, though the merchant himself was blissfully ignorant. When the amber cracked and fell away, Godric opened his eyes.\n\nDust cascaded. His limbs, unused for ten millennia, moved without stiffness. He stood, and the sanctuary groaned around him. Blake stumbled back, hands raised. \u201cWhoa! Okay, you\u2019re alive. That\u2019s\u2026 that\u2019s a lot of muscle for a corpse. Are you okay? How long have you been in there?\u201d\n\n\u201cTen thousand years.\u201d Godric\u2019s voice was gravel, but it smoothed as he used it. \u201cWhat is your name?\u201d\n\n\u201cBlake. I trade\u2014used to trade\u2014textiles. Look, can we get out of this creepy place? My wife\u2019s going to kill me for being late.\u201d\n\nGodric stepped past him, into a world he had already consumed with his awareness. Thronegate\u2019s capital gleamed in the distance, a testament to stolen glory. The king was a boy named Robert, seated on a throne of polished lies. Godric felt the ice crackle.\n\n\u201cBlake,\u201d he said, \u201cdo you know what Thronegate took from me?\u201d\n\n\u201cNo, sir. I don\u2019t even know your name.\u201d\n\n\u201cI am Godric. Once King of Olympus. I had a wife. Two daughters. A friend. They died so this empire could stand. I intend to collect the debt.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s face went pale. \u201cThat\u2026 that sounds like a very large debt.\u201d\n\n\u201cIt is. But I will need only three days.\u201d\n\nThe challenge went out without sound. Godric\u2019s will became a whisper that slithered into every mind across the galaxy. *King Robert of Thronegate. In three days, I will destroy your army. On the fourth day, you will abdicate or die.*\n\n\u2014\n\nThe waiting was tedious. Godric spent it with Blake\u2019s family: Anna, sharp-tongued and unafraid; Josh, a serious twelve-year-old who played chess with a killer\u2019s instinct; Rhea, eight, who collected beetles and offered him a dead one as a gift. \u201cFor luck,\u201d she said. Godric held the fragile carapace in his palm and felt a splinter in the ice. But only a splinter.\n\nOn the morning of battle, the plains outside the capital were a sea of might. Godric stood on a hill, Blake and Anna at his side at his insistence. \u201cYou should witness what I am,\u201d he told them. \u201cAnd what they made me.\u201d\n\nBelow, Thronegate\u2019s army covered every inch of ground. Billions of super-soldiers stood in phalanxes, their genetic enhancements making them demigods. Each wore armor that could survive supernovas, and each carried weapons that could crack worlds. Behind them, mage battalions wove spells that bent probability, froze time, and summoned anti-reality. Mechanical titans strode on legs of gravitational repulsion, their chest-cannons loaded with compressed singularities. In the skies, dragons older than civilizations beat wings that stirred hurricane winds; some could reverse causality in a localized field, making it so their attacks had already landed before they were launched. And in the folds of shadow, ninja clans moved through frozen moments, able to strike from anywhen.\n\nTheir confidence was a physical force. Godric tasted it on the wind: the absolute certainty of victory.\n\nHe folded his arms. He did not move.\n\nHe simply *decided*.\n\nThe first rank of super-soldiers experienced not death, but *uncreation*. Their bodies inverted along dimensional axes they didn\u2019t know they possessed. Skin became internal, organs turned outward, and then the whole mess dissolved into a quantum foam that screamed. Godric let the scream carry\u2014it was important that the others hear it. The mages tried to counter. He made their spells rot in their hands. Fire became frost that shattered their bones; teleportation scattered them across light-years in screaming chunks; the ones who attempted temporal loops found themselves trapped in a recursion of their own deaths, living the same fatal second until their minds broke.\n\nThe mechanical titans fired their singularities. Godric caught the black holes with a thought and whispered them back into the guns that birthed them. The machines crumpled inward, matter and antimatter canceling into silence.\n\nThe dragons he unmade scale by scale. Each plate of armor, each beast, became a separate nerve ending that he set ablaze with a pain that had no physical limit. They rained from the sky like burning mountains, their death throes carving canyons into the earth.\n\nThe ninjas he allowed to complete their ambush. They appeared behind him, blades frozen mid-swing. Godric wrapped them in a time loop that made the moment of their failure eternal. They would spend forever reaching for his neck and never touching it, their minds fully aware.\n\nThere was no blood. No bodies. Godric found the mess distasteful. He erased the evidence, leaving the plain clean and empty. The entire engagement lasted three minutes. Beside him, Blake had fallen to his knees, vomiting bile. Anna was weeping, her face twisted into an expression Godric couldn\u2019t categorize.\n\nHe looked at them, and the splinter in the ice shifted. \u201cIt is done,\u201d he said, and his voice was softer than he intended.\n\n\u2014\n\nTwo days later, Robert\u2019s body was found hanging from the chandelier in his throne room. Godric entered the capital and sat on the throne. The crown felt heavier than it should.\n\nHis first act was the Awakening. He touched the minds of every Thronegate man and spoke the decree: from this day, for every day lived past twenty, their strength, endurance, intelligence, and wisdom would increase tenfold. They could suppress it, live as normal men, but they were now his legion. Women would be protected with an absolute, almost paranoid ferocity; any violation would be met with a response so swift and final the concept of harming a woman would become alien. The people, to his distant surprise, did not cower. They cheered. They called him savior. The men who had once served Robert wept with gratitude. Godric realized, with a strange flicker, that he had become not just a conqueror, but a king.\n\nFor Blake, he made an exception. The merchant\u2019s gift was cut from a deeper cloth: a thousandfold increase instead of ten. Godric wove it into him without explanation, ensuring the modification would pass to Blake\u2019s male descendants should they ever serve. \u201cYou are my friend,\u201d he said when Blake sputtered protests. \u201cI will not lose you to age or weakness.\u201d\n\n\u2014\n\nThe subjugations began soon after. Thronegate\u2019s expansion was not a campaign; it was an inevitability.\n\nThe Crystalline Concordance had prepared for five years. Their seers had glimpsed a \u201chungering void\u201d and they had built dimension-ripping cannons, chronomantic legions, and moonships that could unmake reality. When five Thronegate men arrived\u2014a baker of fifty-two, a smith of forty-seven, a teacher of sixty-one, a farmer of fifty-five, and a musician of forty-three\u2014the Concordance laughed. The men were kindly, even apologetic; they offered the terms of surrender with embarrassed smiles, genuine in their hope that violence could be avoided.\n\nThe Concordance refused, unleashing every weapon at once. The five men stopped suppressing their power.\n\nThe baker raised a flour-dusted hand, and a moon-sized warship split like overripe fruit. The smith kicked the ground with a boot still smelling of forge-fire, and a continent cracked from crust to mantle. The teacher\u2014a gentle man who wept at sad stories\u2014spoke a single word, and the chronomancers found their time-loops turned against them, trapping their armies in eternal stasis. The farmer waved his hand as if shooing flies, and the dimension-ripping cannons crumpled into harmless origami. The musician hummed a lullaby, and the sound unraveled the will of an entire civilization, leaving soldiers catatonic and weeping.\n\nTwenty-seven minutes after it began, the Concordance was a smoking ruin, its leaders on their knees. The five men wept as they accepted the surrender. They were not warriors; they were fathers, husbands, brothers, doing what their king had asked. Godric watched through his omniscience, and the splinter in the ice twisted\u2014a mix of approval and a faint, unwelcome echo of guilt he did not fully understand.\n\n\u2014\n\nThe Magisterium of Eternal Arrogance was less fortunate. They returned Thronegate\u2019s envoys in boxes, their heads arranged in a mocking sigil. Godric was at dinner with Blake\u2019s family when the report reached him. He set down his fork. \u201cExcuse me a moment.\u201d\n\nHe did not rise. He did not gesture. He simply *unmade* the Magisterium. Every dimension, every star, every living soul\u2014folded to a dimensionless point and erased. He left one planet, the one that had sent the heads, suspended in a void where its cosmos had been, so the survivors could forever contemplate their impertinence. The entire act took less than a fraction of a second.\n\nGodric picked up his fork. \u201cThe roast is excellent, Anna.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s face was a mask of horror. \u201cYou\u2014they\u2019re just gone? You didn\u2019t even\u2026 you just erased an entire universe because they were rude?\u201d\n\n\u201cThey were impolite,\u201d Godric said, and there was no apology in his tone. The ice was still thick, the monster still raw. But later that night, he found himself standing outside Blake\u2019s daughter\u2019s bedroom, listening to Rhea hum a tune, and he did not go in. He was not yet ready to be the man he used to be.\n\n\u2014\n\nThe Coalition of Ascended Minds was the most instructive failure. The beings were abstract: living concepts that had never known defeat, existing above the notion of individuality. They observed Godric\u2019s slaughter of the Magisterium and concluded, with the arrogance of the truly ancient, that Godric had a weakness. His emotional history\u2014the trauma of his family\u2019s death. They reasoned that if they could rewrite that foundational memory, they could unmake his power or render him catatonic. They spent decades crafting a psychic lattice that could overwrite conceptual memory at the most fundamental level. They were thorough. They were certain.\n\nThe exact picosecond the first Ascended Mind formed the thought *His grief is a vulnerability we can exploit*, the Weakness Paradox fired. Godric felt it as a warm hum, a pleasant ripple cascading through his infinite layers. His amplification rate, already beyond all measurement, lurched into a new paradigm that made the previous state seem like absolute zero. Every shred of the lattice\u2019s intended function was instantly analyzed, immunized, and mastered. He became impervious to the attack before it was an attack. He gained complete, perfect mastery over conceptual memory alteration\u2014so complete that he could now rewrite the entire Coalition\u2019s history with a stray thought.\n\nHe let them proceed. Curiosity was a rare spice, and he wanted to taste their despair.\n\nThe lattice touched the edge of his awareness. For a flicker, Godric allowed the false memory to bloom: Reina laughing in the garden, Isabel\u2019s small hand in his, Hebe\u2019s mischievous grin as she hid her lucky boot. It was beautiful and exquisitely painful\u2014a poison wrapped in nostalgia. And then Godric exhaled, and the lattice shattered like spun sugar.\n\nHe pulled the Coalition into his mind and showed them the shape of his being. They saw the infinite recursion, the amplification that had no ceiling, the paradox that had already sealed their fate the moment they had first conceived him flawed. They realized, with a agony that transcended time, that their very planning had been feeding him. Every hour they\u2019d spent designing the lattice had deepened his strength, hardened his immunity, and handed him their own weapons. They had not been preparing a victory; they had been forging the chains of their own annihilation.\n\n\u201cYou assumed a flaw,\u201d Godric told them, his voice the quiet of a collapsing star. \u201cYou assumed I could be measured. That assumption was your end.\u201d He erased them. Not just their forms, but their concepts, their history, their potential to ever have existed. He then, as an afterthought, forbade reality from generating such beings again. The omniverse itself seemed to shudder in acquiescence.\n\nBlake, present in the observation chamber, did not speak for a long while. Finally, he said, \u201cYou\u2019re never going to be normal, are you?\u201d\n\n\u201cNo,\u201d Godric said, and there was a weariness in it now. \u201cBut I have you to remind me that I could be worse.\u201d\n\n\u2014\n\nThose words proved to be the turning point. Over the years that followed, Blake became the anchor that pulled Godric back from the abyss. The merchant\u2014now a noble, an advisor, and against all his protests, a burgeoning student of magic\u2014treated Godric not as an untouchable god, but as a man who had been shattered and was slowly, painfully, learning to piece himself together. He pushed back when Godric\u2019s punishments grew too cruel. He laughed at the king\u2019s seriousness and dragged him to family dinners where the conversation was about crop yields and Rhea\u2019s new beau. He insisted that Godric attend court sessions without using his omniscience, so that he would have to listen\u2014truly listen\u2014to his people.\n\nGodric, to his own surprise, obeyed. The ice thawed in stages. He found himself laughing at Blake\u2019s stupid jokes, then at Josh\u2019s dry wit as the boy grew into a man with an uncanny talent for spellcraft. He taught Rhea chess and lost on purpose. When Anna fell ill with a wasting disease that his omniscience had warned him of years in advance, he did not simply cure her with a thought. He sat by her bed, held her calloused hand, and spoke to her about the garden she used to keep, and when she wept from pain, he wept too\u2014a silent, unfamiliar thing that left him raw.\n\nBy the year 20, Godric walked through the capital and his subjects did not just bow; they smiled. Children ran up to him, calling him \u201cUncle King,\u201d and he would kneel to inspect a dead beetle or admire a chalk drawing. He rebuilt the old traditions of Olympus\u2014the harvest festivals, the blessing of newborns\u2014and when a baker\u2019s child died of a fever that he could have prevented had he been paying attention, he attended the funeral not as a god, but as a grieving neighbor. The horror of his power was ever-present; the omniverse still trembled at his name, and any who dared oppose him met an end that defied description. But to those inside his circle, the monster had become a man again\u2014still capable of infinite cruelty, but now choosing warmth.\n\nWhen Blake officially accepted the position of court wizard, the ceremony was small, held in the newly-built tower that overlooked the city. Godric stood behind his friend, adjusting the ceremonial robe on stubborn shoulders. Blake\u2019s mutton chop had gone mostly gray, but his eyes were still sharp, still skeptical. \u201cI still say you\u2019re making a mistake. I can barely light a candle without setting my beard on fire.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou are the descendant of the greatest wizard I ever knew,\u201d Godric said, his voice measured, just loud enough for Blake to catch. \u201cYou carry his blood, his talent, and his stubbornness. You are exactly where you belong.\u201d\n\nBlake frowned, turning halfway. \u201cI\u2019m a merchant\u2019s son. My father sold cloth.\u201d\n\n\u201cYou are my friend.\u201d Godric ignored the question in his eyes\u2014the question he would never answer\u2014and stepped back to let the court applaud. Josh, now a man of twenty-eight, stood in the front row with pride glowing on his face; Rhea, married and pregnant, wiped a tear. The line of Thorin continued, unknowing, in service to the crown.\n\nThat night, Godric stood on the balcony of the palace and looked up at the stars. His omniscience showed him the omniverse in its infinite complexity: the worlds that loved him, the worlds that schemed, the worlds that did not yet know his name. He felt the amplification still churning in his core, the ever-growing list of apocalyptic powers, the sentinel paradox waiting to punish the next fool who dared think him vulnerable. He could end it all with a thought. He could remake existence in any image he chose. Instead, he went back inside, where Rhea\u2019s toddler daughter toddled up and called him \u201cUncle Godric.\u201d He scooped her up and spun her until she shrieked with laughter, and the sound was a balm.\n\nGrief never left him. It was a scar that would never fade, a cold hollow where Reina\u2019s laugh and Isabel\u2019s smile and Hebe\u2019s mischief had once lived. But he had learned to carry it, and to let other things grow around it. He was still the apex predator of the omniverse, still the impossible god who could crush galaxies with a yawn. But to the merchant who had freed him, to the family that had adopted him, to the citizens who trusted him with their lives, he was simply their king. And that, Godric decided, was a purpose worth the endless centuries."

Now he is a shell. He sits in the chair by the window, but he never looks out. His eyes are hollow. He mutters about \"the weight, the weight of his eyes.\" I ask him what happened that day. Godric is the kindest ruler we've ever known. I've seen him in the market, laughing with children. He once healed a farmer's broken leg just by passing by. I can't even look at it without my own mind fracturing.\"\n\nAttempt 2: I found a relic, the Crystal of Serenity, said to cure any mental affliction. I paid a fortune. I placed it on Rogr's chest. The crystal began to vibrate, then to emit a sound like a million screaming insects, and then it imploded into a fine dust. The dust spelled out the word \"NAUGHT\" on the table before fading.\n\nAttempt 3: I tried to get a court wizard's attention indirectly. I sent a petition to the palace medical council. The day my petition was to be reviewed, the building spontaneously developed a localized reality collapse. The wing where the committee sat vanished into a non-space for three hours, and when it returned, the members had forgotten they ever received the petition. The files were blank.\n\nAttempt 4: I took Rogr to a holy site of the Old Gods, thinking maybe the king's power was not absolute there. We knelt in prayer. The statues of the gods crumbled as we approached. The air itself seemed to retreat. A voice, not audible, said: \"Do not bring His attention here. We cannot bear it.\"\n\nThese failures drive me to despair. My love for Rogr is deep, and watching him fade is a slow death. And yet, my frustration never turns against Godric. I can't. It's like being angry at the sun for being bright; it's simply impossible. The king is the source of all order, all goodness. This must be some terrible accident. But I also feel a creeping, nameless dread. If a fraction of his displeasure could do this to my husband, what else could he do?\n\nAfter ten years, Blake arrives. I know Blake by reputation: the king's best friend, the High Court Wizard. He looks older, tired, his mutton chop gray. He knocks on our door. He is polite, hesitant. He says he's there to apologize. He explains: \"It was my idea. I told Godric to play the tyrant, just for a laugh. He didn't mean any harm. He thought it would be a small joke, and then he'd drop it. But he's... he's so far beyond us that even his smallest expressions are cataclysmic. He didn't realize. And I didn't realize. I only found out about your husband ten years later when Godric mentioned it offhand. He thought Rogr would 'tough it out.' He genuinely believed in his resilience.\"\n\nI feel a storm of emotions: anger at Blake, a flash of something like protest against Godric, but still no actual blame. It's a tangled mess. Pete is furious at first, but then he says, \"The king didn't mean it. The king is still good.\" Blake asks our permission to let Godric heal Rogr. He says Godric wants to make it right, but only if we allow it.\n\nWe deliberate. Rogr, for once, speaks clearly: \"I want to be whole. I want to stop being the thing that was noticed.\" We agree. The instant we all say yes, the air pressure changes. Godric is standing in our living room. I didn't see him arrive; he simply was.\n\nDescribe him: he looks like a 45-year-old man, ruggedly handsome, short salt-and-pepper hair and beard, muscular. He's wearing a simple tunic. He could be a neighbor. But my body reacts before my mind: my knees want to buckle, a cold sweat erupts. It's not fear exactly; it's like gravity intensifying. He raises a hand slightly, and the sensation eases. \"My apologies,\" he says, his voice warm, almost fatherly. \"I forget to compensate.\"\n\nHe turns to Rogr. \"I'm sorry for the discomfort. Blake tells me I overdid it. I tend to forget scale.\" He doesn't move or gesture. He simply looks at Rogr, and Rogr gasps. I watch my husband's eyes clear for the first time in ten years. Color rushes back into his cheeks. His hunched posture straightens. He looks twenty years younger, but not de-aged\u2014just impossibly healthy, like a man who has never known sickness or sorrow. The hollows are gone. He looks at me, and he smiles. It is the smile I married. I burst into sobs.\n\nGodric smiles, a small, genuine smile. \"There. That should have been handled a decade ago. I underestimated the fragility.\" He says it with a slight regret, like a man who stepped on a flower. Then he turns to me. \"You tried very hard, Rosa. The crystal was an interesting choice, but it couldn't withstand the residue. I'm sorry you had to go through that.\"\n\nHe offers compensation: \"I can grant you any desire. A new home on a paradise world? Immortality for you and your family? A universe of your own? Ask, and it's yours. I owe you a debt for my oversight.\"\n\nI look at him, and my mind is a battlefield. I just saw him undo ten years of suffering with less effort than breathing. The same being whose casual joke had ruined my husband. The healer who could remake reality. The tyrant and the savior. I love him. I fear him. I want to kneel and kiss his feet, and I want to scream. But I also know that taking nothing from him would preserve something of my own soul.\n\nI decline. Politely. He nods, completely unsurprised, as if he'd already known I'd refuse. \"As you wish,\" he says, and the warmth in his voice is so sincere that my heart aches. Then he is gone. No flash, no sound. He just ceases to be there.\n\nAfterwards, Rogr is himself again. Pete is ecstatic, and he talks about having witnessed a miracle. I should be purely joyful. But I am not. That night, I lie awake, and I watch Rogr sleep peacefully. And I think about the ease of it all. The casual way Godric fixed him. The fact that his offer of a universe was like me offering a slice of bread. The vast, terrifying gulf between him and us. And I realize that my love for him, and my dread, are not contradictory. They are the same thing.\n\nA week later, I overhear a conversation at the market. Godric is walking with Blake, and I am nearby, unseen. Godric says, \"The prank worked out in the end. We should plan another one. Maybe next time, I can pretend to be a beggar king. The look on their faces!\" Blake's reaction is immediate, his voice tight with anger: \"No. Absolutely not. Are you insane? After what happened to Rogr?\" And Godric just laughs, a warm, unbothered sound. \"Blake, you worry too much. I'll be careful.\" And I realize he truly doesn't understand the horror. He might never. And yet, he is still our king, our protector, our god. And my heart is his.\n\nThat ending hits the cognitive dissonance.\n\nNow, we need to write this out in full prose, 3000-3500 words. Use rich sensory language. Ground everything.                     "text": "The seeds of the false poultice had cost me six months of silence and savings. I had ground them with a pestle of petrified whisperwood while reciting the seven invocations of Mending, learned from a crone whose price was a lock of hair from a woman who had never known sorrow. I had no such lock, so I gave her one of mine and prayed the lie would hold. Now, as I pressed the glistening paste to Rogr\u2019s temples, he did not react. He never did.\n\nThe paste warmed. Then it curdled, fast, as if something inside it had panicked. Black threads squirmed across the surface of his skin, and then the entire poultice flaked off in a dusty sigh, taking three layers of his flesh with it. The wounds were clean, bloodless, and perfectly dry, like parchment left too long in a sun that did not exist. Rogr simply sat in the chair by the window, eyes directed at a sky he never commented on, fingers restlessly stroking the armrest as if searching for a thread of a conversation that had ended ten years ago.\n\nI did not cry. I had used up my tears somewhere around the fourth failed attempt, the one with the singing stones that had screamed and shattered, leaving a scar on my forearm that still glowed faintly violet at dusk. Instead, I knelt and wiped the desiccated flakes from his lap, and I told him the lie I always told. \u201cWe\u2019ll try something else. Something quieter.\u201d\n\nHe blinked. His lips moved, and the words came, slow and identical to a thousand other days. \u201cHe was displeased. Just for a heartbeat. The whole weight of existing turned and looked at me, and I wasn\u2019t ready. I\u2019m still not ready.\u201d\n\nI knew the \u201cHe\u201d he meant. Everyone did. The name was not spoken casually in our house, not out of fear, but out of a reverence so deep it had become a physical density in the air. Godric. The Undying King. The Architect of the Awakening. The warm smile in the market square, the gentle hand on a weeping child\u2019s head, the voice that had once\u2014so the stories said\u2014apologized to a baker for making the bread rise too fast. I had seen him myself on two occasions: once during the Remembrance festival, where he\u2019d walked among us with a cup of ale and laughed at a juggler\u2019s poor aim, and once when he\u2019d paused his processional litter to help an old woman who\u2019d dropped her basket of pears. His hands, thick with muscle and callus, had gathered the fruit with such care I had wept for no reason I could name.\n\nThat was the king I knew. That was the king I loved with the same reflexive loyalty that blood owes a heart. So when I looked at Rogr, my husband of twenty-three years, the man who used to recite bad poetry into my hair at dawn, and saw only a husk whose mind had been hollowed out by something I could not see, the contradiction was a thorn I could not pull.\n\nHe\u2019d been a delegate from the newly subjugated Haelstrom worlds. Ten years ago, the surrender had been signed in a hail of bureaucratic exhaustion, and Rogr\u2014steady, eloquent Rogr\u2014had been chosen to present the oaths of fealty to the Thronegate court. He\u2019d been proud. I remember the morning he left, how he\u2019d adjusted the ceremonial collar three times and joked that he\u2019d finally meet the god who\u2019d conquered infinity. He\u2019d meant it in awe. He\u2019d always been a quietly devout man, his faith grounded in the observable fact that the roads were safe, the children well-fed, and the taxes merciful. He believed in Godric\u2019s goodness as a farmer believes in the soil. It was not a question. It was the foundation.\n\nHe came back two weeks later, and he had not spoken a full sentence since.\n\nThe first healer I consulted was a woman named Vex, a mind-walker of considerable repute who operated out of a drifting asteroid in the Seam between multiverses. Her fee had been a year\u2019s wages, paid in advance, and she had arrived through a portal that stank of burnt sugar. I watched her lay her long fingers on Rogr\u2019s forehead, her eyes rolling back until only the bloodshot whites showed. For a full minute, nothing happened. Then she screamed\u2014a high, fluting sound that seemed to bend inward, like a bird being sucked down a drain\u2014and she collapsed. When she woke three hours later, her hair had gone the color of old bone, and her hands trembled too badly to hold a cup of water.\n\n\u201cThere is no wound,\u201d she said, her voice a rustling thing. \u201cHe was\u2026 noticed. The Noticing is still there. It\u2019s like a fingerprint pressed into the soft wax of his being, but the finger belonged to something that has no size and no limit. I tried to look at it. I cannot describe what looked back. It was not cruelty. It was not anger. It was just\u2026 attention. And the smallest possible weight of that attention is still crushing him, every second, because he knows he was seen, and he knows he was found wanting, and the wanting was so infinitesimal that it has no end.\u201d She refused payment, said the memories she\u2019d glimpsed would cost her a decade of her own sanity, and left through a portal she could barely shape.\n\nI did not understand the half of what she said. I still worshipped Godric. I still believed the king was just and kind. The dissonance was a buzzing in my skull that I could not silence.\n\nThe relic came a year later: a crystalline sphere called the Eye of Serenity, said to cleanse any mental affliction by absorbing the trauma into an endless recursion of peace. I traded my mother\u2019s ancestral star-chart for it, a decision that made me a ghost in my own bloodline. I placed the sphere on Rogr\u2019s chest one night, and at first it glowed a gentle blue. I dared to hope. Then the glow curdled into a pulsing black, and the sphere began to vibrate so violently that the windows cracked. It spoke\u2014not in a voice, but in a direct imposition of meaning onto my mind, a single word: NAUGHT. The sphere collapsed into a pinpoint of nothing and was gone, leaving a cold oval of emptiness on Rogr\u2019s chest that took an hour to warm.\n\nI tried petitioning the palace healers indirectly, writing letters that never arrived. The day my final petition was scheduled for review, the administrative wing where the committee sat experienced a localized reality collapse. It was not destructive; the building simply\u2026 stopped existing for three hours. When it returned, the clerks inside had no memory of the event and, more importantly, no memory of any petition regarding a man named Rogr. The files were blank. The ink had fled the paper like insects before a flame.\n\nI dragged Rogr to a holy site of the Old Gods, a ring of standing stones on a world so remote it had no name. The moment we stepped inside the circle, the stones began to bleed from invisible pores, and a pressure built that shoved us back out. A voice, not audible but directly given, said: \u201cDo not bring His attention here. We are not strong enough to be in its path. Your husband carries a reflection. Even the reflection is too bright for us to bear.\u201d The stones then sank into the ground, burying themselves, leaving only a flat expanse of black soil that smoked faintly for days.\n\nThe worst was the charm-binder, a man whose own soul had been replaced with a lattice of adaptive enchantments. He swore he could create a protective amulet strong enough to isolate Rogr\u2019s mind from the weight of the Noticing. He took my measurements, my every last coin, and a cup of Rogr\u2019s blood\u2014and then, mid-incantation, his enchantments began to unravel. The lattice replacing his soul inverted, folded into a Klein-bottle of screaming geometry, and his body followed. I watched him twist into a shape that had no right to exist in three dimensions, his mouth forming a silent O before he and his entire workshop imploded into a sphere the size of a marble. The marble rolled to my foot and was hot to the touch. I left it there.\n\nEach failure deepened the dark, sticky terror that pooled under my daily life. But I never, not once, blamed Godric. How could I? He was the sun. If the sun cast a shadow that swallowed my husband, it was not the sun\u2019s cruelty; it was my own failure to stand in the right place. That was what I told myself. And because I loved the king, because I had seen him lift a child from a well and return her to her mother with a smile that could have calmed a hurricane, I kept my horror folded small and tidy.\n\nOur son Pete was the other tether. He had grown up in Godric\u2019s Thronegate, his entire life a testament to the king\u2019s order. At eighteen, he was blazing with the same devotion I felt, but raw and uncomplicated. He kept a portrait of Godric in his room, not the official icon of the crown, but a charcoal sketch he\u2019d done himself after seeing the king speak at a festival. He would point to it when visitors came. \u201cThat\u2019s Him,\u201d he\u2019d say, with a reverence that bordered on prayer. \u201cHe gave us the Awakening. He made the universe safe. My father was blessed to meet Him.\u201d\n\nWhenever he said that, I would watch Rogr\u2019s face. There was no flicker. No recognition. But once, after Pete had gone to bed, Rogr whispered, \u201cSafe. Yes. We are safe. That\u2019s what makes it so hard to breathe. The safety itself is so big it leaves no room for anything else.\u201d I pressed my hand to his cheek, and he leaned into it like a child, and we sat that way until dawn.\n\nThe year was 38, and Rogr had been a shade for a decade, when Blake knocked on our door.\n\nI recognized him immediately. The High Court Wizard, the right hand of God, the man whose name was spoken with a fondness that eclipsed nearly every other figure save the king himself. His mutton chop had grayed, and his eyes carried the same deep lines of someone who had looked too long at things that were not meant to be survived. He wore ordinary merchant\u2019s wool, and he bowed to me as if I were a duchess.\n\n\u201cMy name is Blake,\u201d he said, though he didn\u2019t need to. \u201cI\u2019ve come to apologize.\u201d\n\nI led him inside, my mind a quiet roar. Pete was out, and Rogr was in his chair. Blake looked at Rogr for a long moment, and his face crumpled in a way that was entirely un-wizardly. \u201cOh,\u201d he said, soft. \u201cOh, Rogr. I\u2019m so sorry.\u201d\n\nThen he told me everything. The words spilled out in a tumble: the delegation ten years ago, the assumption among the new subjects that Godric was a merciless tyrant, and the offhand joke Blake had made. \u201cI told him, \u2018Why not play the tyrant for a bit, just for fun? Let them see the mask before you show the face.\u2019 I meant it as a prank. A harmless bit of theatre. Godric trusted me. He took my advice. He met your husband and the other delegates and he\u2026 he pretended mild displeasure. A fraction of a fraction of a sliver of annoyance. For him, it was like frowning at a fly. But for Rogr\u2026\u201d Blake\u2019s voice cracked. \u201cGodric doesn\u2019t always understand scale. He held back nearly all of himself, but even that infinitesimal remainder was the unclothed attention of an omnipotent being. It landed on your husband, and it crushed something that doesn\u2019t grow back.\u201d\n\nMy first emotion was not anger. It was a strange, dizzying relief. There was a reason. There was a cause. The contradiction that had been eating me for a decade finally had a shape. I stared at Blake, and I tried to find rage, but all I found was the same buzzing, that awful cognitive whine. \u201cHe didn\u2019t mean it,\u201d I said, my voice scraping. \u201cHe thought it was a joke.\u201d\n\n\u201cHe did,\u201d Blake said, and the guilt in his voice was a physical weight. \u201cAnd I suggested it. I found out about Rogr only last week. Godric mentioned it casually\u2014\u2018The Haelstrom delegate, the one who took it hard, he\u2019s still struggling.\u2019 Just like that. He\u2019d known the whole time. He thought Rogr would tough it out. He believes in mortal resilience, you see. He was mortal once, a long time ago, before Olympus fell. He thinks we\u2019re stronger than we are. He underestimated, and I never bothered to check. I\u2014\u201d\n\nHe stopped, swallowed, and knelt before Rogr, something a High Court Wizard should never do. \u201cI am responsible. I have come to ask your forgiveness, and your permission. I want to bring Godric here to heal you. He wants to. But he won\u2019t act without your consent.\u201d\n\nRogr\u2019s head lifted. For the first time in a decade, his eyes focused. The movement was so unexpected I nearly fell. \u201cConsent,\u201d Rogr repeated, and the word was rusty, dragged from a deep well. \u201cHe wants my permission?\u201d\n\n\u201cYes,\u201d Blake said. \u201cHe insists.\u201d\n\nPete had come home silently, standing in the doorway with his drawing satchel, his face pale. He looked at his father, then at the High Court Wizard kneeling on our threadbare rug, and he said, \u201cIf the king wants to help, we should let him.\u201d\n\nRogr was silent for a heartbeat, then two. Then he nodded, a single fragile dip of his chin. \u201cI want to stop being the thing that was noticed,\u201d he said. \u201cI want to be Rogr again. Tell him\u2026 tell him I would like to be whole.\u201d\n\nThe air in the room did not shift; it *submitted*. There was no flash, no sound, no portal. Godric was simply standing beside the hearth, as if he\u2019d always been there and we\u2019d only just noticed. He was a man of forty-five, ruggedly handsome, with a salt-and-pepper beard and short hair, his body a monument of controlled muscle beneath a plain gray tunic. He could have been anyone\u2019s favorite uncle, except for the way the light bent toward him, as if eager to serve.\n\nMy knees hit the floor before I consciously commanded them. Pete dropped his satchel and bowed so deep his forehead touched the boards. Blake, still kneeling, ducked his head. Only Rogr remained seated, but he was trembling, his eyes wide and filling with a terror that was also hope.\n\n\u201cPlease,\u201d Godric said, his voice a warm baritone, \u201cnone of that. Rosa, get up. I\u2019m not here as a king. I\u2019m here to fix a mistake I should have corrected years ago.\u201d He smiled at me, and it was the same smile I\u2019d seen in the market, the one that made old women weep and children giggle. There was no trace of the tyrant. There was only a man whose gentleness was so absolute it terrified me more than any anger could.\n\nHe turned to Rogr. \u201cMy friend Blake tells me I owe you an apology. I\u2019m sorry, Rogr. I thought you would shake it off. I misjudged. Sometimes I forget what it\u2019s like to be breakable. That\u2019s not an excuse; it\u2019s a failure of memory. May I touch you?\u201d\n\nRogr\u2019s answer was a choked sob. Godric did not move, did not reach out, did not gesture. He simply *decided*, and the healing occurred. I did not see light or feel warmth; there was no special effect. One moment Rogr was a crumbled effigy of a man, and the next he was whole. The hollows under his eyes filled. The gray pallor of his skin flushed with the robust color of a man who has never missed a meal or a night\u2019s sleep. His shoulders squared, his spine straightened, and his breath came in a deep, easy rhythm that I had not heard in ten years. He didn\u2019t de-age; he simply became the picture of health, a vitality so radiant it seemed to hum. The memory of the trauma was still there\u2014I could see it in the quiet shadow that lingered behind his eyes\u2014but the weight of it was gone. He was Rogr again. My Rogr.\n\nI was on him in a heartbeat, my arms around his neck, my face buried in his hair, which smelled of him instead of the stale nothing it had held for a decade. He was laughing, a wet, bewildered sound, and his hands came up to grip my back with a strength I had forgotten. \u201cI\u2019m here,\u201d he said, over and over. \u201cI\u2019m here, I\u2019m here, I\u2019m here.\u201d\n\nPete was weeping, a young man\u2019s ugly, unguarded sob. He clutched at his father\u2019s arm and pressed his forehead to Rogr\u2019s shoulder, and Blake stood back, his face a mess of relief and residual guilt.\n\nGodric watched the reunion with a small, pleased smile. Then his gaze shifted to me. \u201cRosa, you went through extraordinary lengths. The Crystal of Serenity, the mind-walker, the petition, the charm-binder. I am aware of every attempt, and I am sorry you had to endure so much failure.\u201d His words were tender, but they landed in my chest like a cold spike. He\u2019d known. He\u2019d known all along, every desperate hour, every shattered relic, every coin I\u2019d bled. He\u2019d watched me crumble piece by piece, believing in my own inadequacy, while he could have fixed it with a thought. And yet he was sorry. And yet he was here. And yet I still loved him so fiercely it bent my spine.\n\n\u201cI would like to offer you compensation,\u201d Godric said, and his tone was that of a neighbor offering to share a cask of ale. \u201cName anything. A new world, tailored to your exact desires, orbiting a star that will never die. Immortality for you, Rogr, and Pete, with bodies that never tire. A personal universe where you can be its sole caretakers. Wealth beyond measurement. Power on the scale of my own court wizards. Whatever you ask, I will grant. I owe you a debt that outweighs any boon.\u201d\n\nThe offer was so astronomically vast that my mind skittered off its surface. He was offering me a universe. The same casual way I might offer a guest a second helping of soup. And I knew, with a certainty that had no logical basis, that he meant every word. The silence in the room was the heavy, wet silence of an ocean before a storm. Pete looked at me, his eyes shining with a wild, hungry hope. Rogr\u2019s hand tightened on mine.\n\nI thought of the stones that had bled. The sphere that had shouted NAUGHT. The healer whose hair turned white. The charm-binder who had folded into a marble. All of that effort, all of that pain, and he could undo it without lifting a finger. The gratitude I felt was real. The love I felt was real. And the dread\u2014the cold, clean dread\u2014was also real, because I understood now that his kindness and his terror were the same thing wearing different clothes. He was the gentle hand that could accidentally crush a world. He was the apology that came after ten years of agony, because the agony was so small to him that it slipped his mind.\n\nI could not take his compensation. Accepting it would feel like letting the universe balance an equation that could never be balanced. It would feel, in some twisted way, like forgiving the existential horror by letting him pay me off. And I did not want to forgive the horror. I wanted to live with it, to hold it alongside the love, because both were true. I wanted my soul to remember that the sun is beautiful and also burns.\n\n\u201cI decline,\u201d I said, my voice steadier than I felt. \u201cWith all gratitude, Your Majesty, I decline.\u201d\n\nGodric nodded, and there was no surprise in his expression, only a quiet, knowing acceptance. \u201cAs you wish, Rosa. You are brave, and your love for your husband is a strength I recognize and respect. The offer will stand, should you ever change your mind.\u201d He looked at Rogr, who met his gaze without flinching. \u201cTake care of her. She is fiercer than any army I\u2019ve faced.\u201d\n\nAnd then he was gone. Not a fade, not a blink. Simply gone, leaving behind the faint scent of ozone and the lingering warmth of a presence that had momentarily made the room feel like the center of all creation.\n\nWe stood in the aftermath, my family whole, my house suddenly too large and too small. Pete launched into a torrent of excited chatter\u2014had we *seen* that, the king had been *in our house*, he\u2019d spoken to *us*\u2014and Rogr held me close, his heart a steady thump against my ear. I should have been purely happy. I was. And I was also not. Because I knew that I would wake up every morning for the rest of my life and love the king who had saved my husband, and every night I would lie awake and remember the casual, terrifying ease of that salvation, and the two truths would grind together like tectonic plates, producing a friction that would never, ever heal.\n\nA week later, the city was preparing for the Remembrance festival. I was in the market, buying bread, when I heard familiar voices in a narrow alley near the baker\u2019s. It was Blake and Godric, walking together, their forms slightly obscured by hanging laundry. I would have retreated, but my feet refused.\n\nGodric was speaking, his voice light with a mischief that made my stomach clench. \u201cYou know, Blake, that prank worked out quite well in the end. Rogr got healed, his family is grateful, and I got to see some real mortal grit. We should plan another one. Maybe I could pretend to be a beggar king next time. Show up in rags and see how the court reacts! The look on their faces would be priceless.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s response was immediate and sharp, his tone carrying the same anger I had seen in my own mirror. \u201cNo. Absolutely not. Are you insane? After what happened to Rogr? After what happened to Rosa? You think this is a game? They suffered for a *decade*, Godric. A decade of hell because of a joke I shouldn\u2019t have made and a power you can\u2019t ever really measure. I\u2019m not doing it again. Find another hobby.\u201d\n\nThere was a pause. Then Godric laughed\u2014a real, genuine, warm laugh. \u201cBlake, you worry too much. I\u2019ll be careful next time. I\u2019ve learned now. I\u2019ll use a smaller fraction. It\u2019ll be fine.\u201d\n\nI stood frozen behind the laundry, a loaf of bread growing cold in my hands. He didn\u2019t understand. He might never understand. And because he was Godric, he didn\u2019t have to. My heart swelled with love for my king, and it curdled with a dread that sat in my throat like a stone. I carried the bread home and did not speak of what I\u2019d heard. What was there to say? The man who could heal Rogr with a thought could also break him again with a frown. And I would love him either way, because that was the nature of being a subject of the Undying King. The terror was the price of the peace. And I, Rosa of Haelstrom, wife of Rogr, mother of Pete, would pay it forever."

Tim hears Godric talk to it like a pet.\n- Evolution: Gent gains a new ability, like the power to retroactively unmake the concept of resistance, or to project an aura of despair that prevents any future rebellion, or it learns how to \"play\" with prey. Godric claps his hands. \"Look, Tim! He's learning!\"\n- Tim's dread: He loves Godric, but he's also terrified of Gent, and more terrified that this is just a fraction of a fraction of Godric's power.\n\nWe need to ensure the story stays within 3500 words, but it's okay to be a bit over if needed, but we'll aim for 3000-3500.\n\nNow, craft the story.\n\nStart with Tim in his study, then summoned by Godric to the observation deck. The being unravels, feeling every piece of its godhood ripped away, a process that takes an eternity in a frozen moment, but objectively an instant. The corpse, if any, is then disintegrated.\n\n2. The Chronos Legion: an army of time-warriors who exist at all points in time simultaneously, able to attack from every moment. They have already killed Godric in the past, they believe. Gent, being omnipresent and omniscient, simply edits their existence from the timeline. They experience their own non-existence as a recursive loop where they are born, live, and then are erased by an outside force that they realize too late is the aura. The horror is that they retain memory of their erased selves.\n\n3. The Null-Throne: a metaphysical weapon that enforces absolute nothingness, a throne that when sat upon, unmakes the multiverse. A being named Khaon sits on it and directs the void to swallow Godric. Gent instead makes the Null-Throne consume itself, turning its void inward. Khaon is trapped in an infinite regression of being unmade and remade, feeling his body dissolve cell by cell, soul by layer, each atom screaming.\n\n4. The Empathy Plague: a psychic virus that spreads through emotional connection, meant to make Godric feel the suffering of all his victims and drive him to self-destruction. Gent isolates the virus, amplifies it a billionfold, and redirects it onto the entire resistance, who all instantly experience the suffering of every being they've ever killed, multiplied by an infinite recursion, until their minds shatter and their bodies follow, resulting in a mass \"meat fountain\" description.\n\nThen briefly describe the rest: the infinite armadas, the conceptual horrors, the reality-benders, all snuffed out in the same fraction of a second.\n\nAfter, the space is clean, not a speck of dust.
